                  <hi rend="ital">He died having passed away from,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">leaving behind him, sons and daughters.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">مَاتَ عَنْ ثَمَانِينَ</foreign>
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَنًة</foreign>
                  <hi rend="ital">He died having passed beyond eighty years;</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">being eighty years old.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">اللَّبَنُ لَا يَمُوتُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The milk will not die</hi>], in a saying of 'Omar, in a trad., means, that if a child sucks the milk of a dead woman, it becomes unlawful for him afterwards to marry any of her relations who would be unlawful to him if he sucked her milk while she was living: or it means, that, if milk taken from the breast of a woman is given to a child to drink, and he drinks it, the consequence is the same; that the effect of the milk in producing this consequence is not annulled by its separation from the breast; for whatever is separated from a living being is termed <foreign lang="ar">ميت</foreign>, or dead, except the milk and hair and wool on account of the necessity of making use of these. MF observes, that <foreign lang="ar">مَيْتٌ</foreign> is asserted to be contracted from <foreign lang="ar">مَيِّتٌ</foreign>; and if so, that there can be no difference in their meanings: that the making a difference between them is contrary to analogy; agreeably with which, they should be like <foreign lang="ar">هَيْنٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هَيِّنٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">لَيْنٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَيِّنٌ</foreign>: and also contrary to what has been heard from the Arabs; for they made no difference in their use of these two words. (Msb.)       <foreign lang="ar">أَرْضٌ <ref cref="n39015-1" target="مَيْتَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (En-Nawawee:) land <hi rend="ital">that has not been sown, nor cultivated, nor occupied by any man's camels &amp;c.:</hi>  
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n39015-2" target="مَوَتَانٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar" select="n39014"/></foreign> signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">مُوَاتٌ</foreign> (<foreign lang="ar">مَوَاتٌ</foreign>?), namely, land <hi rend="ital">that is no man's property;</hi> and is also written <foreign lang="ar">مَوْتَانٌ</foreign>: (L:) or <foreign lang="ar">مَوَتَانٌ</foreign> signifies land <hi rend="ital">that has not yet been brought into a state of cultivation:</hi> (Fr, S, L, K:) in a trad. it is said, that such land is the property of God and his Apostle; and whosoever brings into a state of cultivation such land, to him it belongs. (S.)    </entryFree>2e:Tcc9,<entryFree id="n39023" key="مُسْتَمِيتٌ" type="main">
                  <form>
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مُسْتَمِيتٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> A <hi rend="ital">courageous</hi> man, <hi rend="ital">who seeks,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">courts death:</hi> (K:) a man <hi rend="ital">who seeks to be slain; who cares not, in war, for death:</hi> (S:) <hi rend="ital">abandon-</hi>
                  <pb n="2743"/>
                  <hi rend="ital">ing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">devoting, himself to death,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">مسْتَرْسِلٌ لِلْمَوْتِ</foreign>,) as also <foreign lang="ar">مُسْتَقْتِلٌ</foreign>. (A.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Abandoning,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">devoting himself to</hi> a thing, or affair; syn. <foreign lang="ar">مُسْتَرْسِلٌ لِأَمْرٍ</foreign>. (S, K.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">هَوَ مُسْتَمِيتٌ إِلَى كَذَا</foreign>, as also <foreign lang="ar">مُسْتَهْلِكٌ</foreign>, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He</hi> [<hi rend="ital">is devoted to such a thing, so that he</hi>] <hi rend="ital">imagines that he shall die if he do not attain it.</hi> (A.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  Ru-beh says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَزَبَدُ البَحْرِ لَهُ كَتِيتُ</foreign>
                     </L>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَاللَّيْلُ فَوْقَ المَاءِ مُسْتَمِيتُ</foreign>
                     </L>
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And to the froth of the sea there was a sound like that of boiling, and night impended over the water</hi>]. (S.) [It is implied in the S that <foreign lang="ar">مستميت</foreign> here signifies <foreign lang="ar">مُسْتَرْسِل</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  One <hi rend="ital">who feigns himself to be insane,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">possessed by a devil; not being really so.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  One <hi rend="ital">who feigns lowliness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">submissiveness, in voice, &amp;c., to this man until he feeds him, and to this until he feeds him, and, when he is satiated, is ungrateful to his benefactors.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  One <hi rend="ital">who makes a show of being good and quiet</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tranquil, and is not so in reality.</hi> (Ibn-El-Mubárak.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مُسْتَمِيتٌ</foreign> The <hi rend="ital">thin pellicle that adheres to the white of an egg.</hi> (K.) [See 10: and see also <foreign lang="ar">مُسْتَمِيثٌ</foreign>, in art. <foreign lang="ar">ميث</foreign>.]
